###xml 87 97 87 97 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Figs. 6C&#8211;E</xref>
###xml 102 104 102 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">8A</xref>
###xml 253 260 253 260 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Fig. 6A</xref>
###xml 386 389 386 389 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 382 389 382 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 390 399 390 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>

###xml 703 707 700 704 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Kwon2">[10]</xref>
###xml 728 732 725 729 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</sub>
###xml 728 732 725 729 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>Ate1</sub></italic>
###xml 763 766 760 763 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 759 766 756 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 876 880 873 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 1082 1085 1079 1082 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1078 1085 1075 1082 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1086 1095 1083 1092 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1148 1151 1145 1148 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1144 1151 1141 1148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1160 1170 1157 1167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g001">Fig. 1C, D</xref>
###xml 1192 1196 1189 1193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 1223 1226 1220 1223 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1219 1226 1216 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1227 1236 1224 1233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1334 1346 1331 1343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s1">Introduction</xref>
###xml 1349 1356 1346 1353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g001">Fig. 1D</xref>
###xml 26 30 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 151 155 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 358 362 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 400 404 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 511 515 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 632 636 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 767 771 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 944 949 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1096 1100 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1237 1241 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Most of Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mice (96 of 180) were strikingly hyperactive (hyperkinetic) (Figs. 6C-E and 8A). Intact brains harvested from Ate1-deficient mice appeared swollen, in comparison to brains harvested, in parallel, from Ate1-containing siblings (Fig. 6A). While the average brain weight, as a percentage of total body weight (TBW), of Ate1-containing mice was 1.96%, that of Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mice was 3.09% (Fig. 6A). In addition, there was a larger scatter of relative brain weights for Ate1-deficient mice, in comparison to identically TM-treated Ate1-containing controls. In particular, the brains of some Ate1-deficient mice reached 5% of TBW (Fig. 6A). Histological patterns of NLS-betagal [10] expressed from the PAte1 promoter in the brains of Ate1+/- mice (data not shown) were in agreement with in situ hybridization data in the Allen Brain Atlas (), in that Ate1 was expressed at varying but significant levels throughout the mouse brain, particularly in the hippocampus, dorsal thalamus, and cerebellum. No Ate1 protein could be detected in brain extracts of Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mice, in contrast to extracts from wild-type or Ate1+/- brains (Fig. 1C, D). The virtually null Ate1 state of the brain in Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mice was also indicated by a strong accumulation of Rgs4, a physiological substrate of Ate1 (see Introduction) (Fig. 1D).
###end p 40

###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 50 53 50 53 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 46 53 46 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 54 63 54 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 912 919 912 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Fig. 6B</xref>
###xml 1247 1257 1247 1257 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Fig. 6A, B</xref>
###xml 64 68 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 572 576 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1050 1054 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We carried out cell proliferation assays with Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mice (and controls), using 5-ethynyl-2'-deoxyuridine (EdU). In examinations of EdU-labeled brain sections, we paid particular attention to regions such as the hippocampus and the periventricular zone of the lateral ventricles, where neurogenesis is known to occur. However, no differences in EdU incorporation between Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing brains were observed (data not shown), consistent with a brain edema (fluid accumulation) being a significant cause of brain enlargement in Ate1-deficient mice. We also determined the water content of freshly isolated brains, by subtracting their "dry weights" (after freeze-drying) from their total weights. The average water content and dry weight of control (Ate1-containing) brains was 79.9% and 20.1%, respectively, versus 80.5% and 19.5%, respectively (p<0.03), for Ate1-deficient brains (Fig. 6B). Thus cerebral edema at least contributes to the observed differences in brain weight between Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing mice. It remains to be determined whether an edema (owing, e.g., to an osmotic imbalance or inflammation) suffices to account for consistently observed Ate1-dependent differences in brain weights (Fig. 6A, B).
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 540 550 516 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">Fig. 8B, C</xref>
###xml 77 81 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 140 144 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 182 186 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 268 272 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 329 333 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 402 406 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 534 538 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
There was also a 10-fold higher propensity for seizures among Ate1-deficient mice. For example, during routine cage changes and handling of mice, approximately3.1% of Ate1-deficient mice (38 of 1,232) versus approximately0.3% of identically TM-treated Ate1-containing mice had tonic-clonic seizures. The skulls of Ate1-deficient mice appeared to be thinner, "softer" than the sculls of Ate1-containing mice. Although MRI analyses did not reveal statistically significant abnormalities in the shape or size of skulls in Ate1-deficient mice (Fig. 8B, C), the MRI data did not preclude the possibility that bone structure may be perturbed in the absence of Ate1. These issues remain to be addressed.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 205 208 205 208 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 367 374 367 374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">Fig. 8D</xref>
###xml 600 610 600 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Figs. 6C&#8211;E</xref>
###xml 615 617 615 617 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">8A</xref>
###xml 670 677 670 677 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">Fig. 8D</xref>
###xml 996 1003 996 1003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Fig. 6C</xref>
###xml 1034 1037 1034 1037 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1030 1037 1030 1037 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1038 1047 1038 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1116 1120 1116 1120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 1120 1123 1120 1123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 1154 1157 1154 1157 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 1150 1157 1150 1157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1158 1167 1158 1167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1201 1207 1201 1207 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/+</sup>
###xml 1197 1207 1197 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1208 1217 1208 1217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1225 1232 1225 1232 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Fig. 6E</xref>
###xml 60 64 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 229 233 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 332 336 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 594 598 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 757 761 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 832 837 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1048 1053 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1125 1130 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1168 1173 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1218 1223 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
The neurological/behavioral abnormalities of Ate1-deficient mice included an enhanced startle response, a marker for increased anxiety in rodents. Specifically, the latency between stimulus and response (Tmax) for Ate1-deficient mice was between 54% and 76% of the average latency for Ate1-containing controls, i.e., Ate1-deficient mice reacted significantly faster (Fig. 8D), thus exhibiting an enhanced startle response. The open field test is used to assess locomotor, exploratory and anxiety-like behavior in rodents. This test revealed a remarkably hyperkinetic behavior of Ate1-deficient mice (Figs. 6C-E and 8A), consistent with their enhanced startled response (Fig. 8D). The initial test involved a 15-min comparison of movements of Ate1-deficient mice versus Ate1-containing siblings of the same litter. An Ate1-deficient mouse traveled, during the test, a 3-fold greater distance than their (identically TM-treated) Ate1-containing counterpart (175.71 m versus 55.63 m, respectively) (Fig. 6C). The mean velocity of an Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mouse was 19.5 cm/sec, in comparison to 7.0 cm/sec for a wild-type (Ate1+/+) mouse, 6.2 cm/sec for an Ate1+/+;CaggCreER mouse, and 5.5 cm/sec for an Ate1flox/+;CaggCreER mouse (Fig. 6E).
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 294 297 294 297 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 290 297 290 297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 410 417 410 417 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">Fig. 8A</xref>
###xml 596 603 596 603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">Fig. 8A</xref>
###xml 107 111 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 213 217 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 393 397 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 552 556 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 678 682 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 860 864 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To assess generality of this striking phenotype, we repeated the open field test with three Ate1-deficient mice at 10, 26, 38, and 82 days after TM treatment, in parallel with TM-treated Ate1-containing (control) mice. At 10 days after TM treatment, i.e., soon after the acquisition of the Ate1-/- genotype, the differences between distances travelled by Ate1-deficient versus Ate1-containing mice were small (Fig. 8A). However, by 26 days after TM treatment, there was a statistically significant difference between Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing mice in regard to their locomotor activity (Fig. 8A). By 82 days after TM treatment, the locomotor activity of Ate1-deficient mice, in conjunction with their elevated overall anxiety, increased so much that the device in which the open field tests were performed became nearly impractical, as Ate1-deficient mice (in contrast to Ate-containing ones) kept jumping out of the testing box.
###end p 46
###begin title 47
###xml 52 56 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Depletion of White Adipose Tissue in Ate1-Deficient Mice, and Their Resistance to Diet-Induced Obesity
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 172 180 172 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g005">Figs. 5D</xref>
###xml 185 189 185 189 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">7A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 468 478 444 454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">Fig. 7D, E</xref>
###xml 732 742 708 718 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g009">Fig. 9A, B</xref>
###xml 114 118 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 166 170 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 296 300 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 402 406 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 539 543 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 776 780 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To address the cause of a strikingly lower content of the peritoneal white adipose tissue (WAT) in Ate1-deficient mice, on average only 16% of WAT in Ate1-containing mice (Figs. 5D and 7A-C), we examined sections of intraperitoneal WAT. The average diameter of WAT adipocytes from Ate1-deficient mice was approximately30% of the average diameter of such cells in identically TM-treated Ate1-containing mice (25.5+/-7.4 microm versus 76.2+/-16.2 microm, respectively) (Fig. 7D, E). Thus, at least the bulk of WAT decrease in Ate1-deficient mice resulted from a decreased lipid content of individual adipocytes, rather from an extensive loss of adipocytes. Similar results were obtained with intrascapular brown adipose tissue (BAT) (Fig. 9A, B). The leanness of Ate1-deficient mice was particularly striking in view of their hyperphagy (see below).
###end p 48
###begin title 49
###xml 69 72 69 72 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 65 72 65 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 84 87 84 87 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 80 87 80 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 88 92 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Body temperature, amino acid utilization and other properties of Ate1-/- versus Ate1+/+ mice.
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 161 167 157 163 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/+</sup>
###xml 157 167 153 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 168 177 164 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>

###xml 297 306 289 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 352 354 344 346 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>

###xml 464 473 456 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 521 527 513 519 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 517 527 509 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 528 537 520 529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 629 631 621 623 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 731 733 723 725 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 757 778 749 770 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 791 793 783 785 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 888 890 880 882 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 139 144 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 268 273 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 434 439 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 500 505 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 826 830 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1031 1035 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1218 1222 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1371 1375 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1420 1424 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1449 1453 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
(A) Hematoxylin/eosin staining (200x magnification) of a 10-microm section of brown adipose tissue (BAT) harvested from an Ate1-containing mouse (TM-treated Ate1flox/+;CaggCreER). The bar denotes 100 microm. (B) Same as in A except that BAT was from an Ate1-deficient mouse (TM-treated Ate1flox/-;CaggCreER). ###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 137 146 137 146 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g004">Fig. 4A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 502 509 502 509 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">Fig. 7F</xref>
###xml 685 695 685 695 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g004">Fig. 4A, B</xref>
###xml 938 945 926 933 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g009">Fig. 9E</xref>
###xml 998 1001 974 977 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 994 1001 970 977 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1002 1011 978 987 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1018 1028 994 1004 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g004">Fig. 4A, B</xref>
###xml 1178 1185 1142 1149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g009">Fig. 9E</xref>
###xml 1237 1246 1201 1210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">Fig. 7A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 1307 1314 1271 1278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g009">Fig. 9F</xref>
###xml 101 105 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 297 301 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 434 438 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 614 618 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 826 830 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1012 1016 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1068 1072 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1157 1161 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1264 1268 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We also asked whether the consistent difference in weight between Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing mice on a standard ad libitum diet (Fig. 4A-C) could be reduced by an energy-rich, high-fat diet (HFD). At the end of the resulting 10-week test, the average weight of HFD-treated Ate1-containing mice was 152% of their starting weight (40.0 g versus 26.3 g). In contrast, the average weight of identically HFD-treated Ate1-deficient mice was only 122% (24.0 g versus 19.7 g) of their starting weight (Fig. 7F), indicating their relative resistance to diet-induced obesity. Yet another phenotype of Ate1-deficient mice, observed during their initial loss of weight after TM treatment (Fig. 4A, B), was their lower core body temperature, on average 35.1degreesC, in comparison to identically TM-treated Ate1-containing control mice, whose average core body temperature was 36.0degreesC during the same time, in the absence of weight loss (Fig. 9E). After the early deaths of approximately15% of Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mice (Fig. 4A, B), the average temperature of surviving mice (36.6degreesC) was not significantly different from that of Ate1-containing control mice (36.7degreesC) (Fig. 9E). As one would expect from their depletion of WAT (Fig. 7A-C), Ate1-deficient mice were strongly hypersensitive to cold (Fig. 9F).
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 351 354 351 354 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 347 354 347 354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 449 453 449 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Kiskinis1">[32]</xref>
###xml 455 459 455 459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Narvaez1">[33]</xref>
###xml 546 550 546 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ucp1</italic>
###xml 658 667 658 667 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">Fig. 7G&#8211;I</xref>
###xml 710 714 710 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ucp1</italic>
###xml 784 793 784 793 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">Fig. 7G&#8211;I</xref>
###xml 908 912 908 912 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Kiskinis1">[32]</xref>
###xml 322 327 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 652 656 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 778 782 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Ucp1 is a proton carrier in the mitochondrial inner membrane that mediates a partial uncoupling of oxidative phosphorylation from ATP synthesis, an alteration that can increase heat production and thereby regulate body temperature and energy homeostasis. Although Ucp1 is normally expressed in BAT but not in WAT, several mouse mutants other than Ate1-/- that are resistant to diet-induced obesity have been shown to ectopically express Ucp1 in WAT [32], [33]. Using RT-PCR and immunoblotting with anti-Ucp1 antibody, we found that the levels of Ucp1 mRNA and Ucp1 protein in BAT did not change significantly between Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing mice (Fig. 7G-I). Remarkably, however, the levels of both Ucp1 mRNA and Ucp1 were strongly increased in WAT of Ate1-deficient mice (Fig. 7G-I). A Ucp1-Ate1 connection revealed by these findings adds a new dimension to the understanding of Ucp1 regulation ([32] and refs. therein), and may also provide an experimental route to identifying a relevant circuit that involves Ate1.
###end p 52
###begin title 53
###xml 43 47 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Increased Metabolic Rate in Ate1-Deficient Mice
###end title 53
###begin p 54
###xml 43 49 43 49 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 39 49 39 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 50 59 50 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 77 83 77 83 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/+</sup>
###xml 73 83 73 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 84 93 84 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 237 245 237 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10C</xref>
###xml 308 311 308 311 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 304 311 304 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 312 321 312 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 427 435 427 435 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10C</xref>
###xml 680 688 668 676 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10C</xref>
###xml 952 956 904 908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 956 959 908 911 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 964 968 916 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 970 971 922 923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</italic>
###xml 968 971 920 923 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/<italic>&#8722;</italic></sup>
###xml 1090 1098 1042 1050 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10C</xref>
###xml 1415 1423 1367 1375 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10A</xref>
###xml 1823 1831 1775 1783 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10B</xref>
###xml 1979 1987 1931 1939 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t002">Tables 2</xref>
###xml 1992 1993 1944 1945 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t003">3</xref>
###xml 95 99 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 322 326 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 421 425 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 496 500 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 822 826 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 972 976 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1011 1015 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1167 1171 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1409 1413 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1441 1445 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1500 1504 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1757 1761 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1806 1810 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1973 1977 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
During the week prior to TM treatment, Ate1flox/-;CaggCreER and control (Ate1flox/+;CaggCreER) mice (at that point, both strains contained Ate1) consumed 0.63 and 0.62 kcal of standard chow per gram of body weight per day, respectively (Fig. 10C). Within a week after TM treatment the now Ate1-deficient Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mice increased their food consumption on average to 125% of identically TM-treated Ate1-containing mice (Fig. 10C). This pattern of significant hyperphagia of Ate1-deficient mice continued for the duration of this study, i.e., up to approximately8 months, with regular measurements for 6 weeks following TM treatment and intermittent comparisons afterwards (Fig. 10C). Thus, despite their initial decline of weight shortly after TM treatment and the early death of approximately15% of Ate1-deficient mice, and despite their subsequent failure to gain, on average, more than approximately63% and approximately69% of the weights of Ate1+/+ and Ate1+/- mice, respectively, the Ate1-deficient mice consumed significantly more food than their Ate1-containing counterparts (Fig. 10C). To address their patterns of glucose utilization, we fasted these mice for 16 hr and measured blood glucose before after administering a 50-mg (0.2 ml) bolus of glucose by gavage. The kinetics of rise and fall of blood glucose levels under these conditions was similar for Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing mice (Fig. 10A). Ate1-deficient mice had lower fasting glucose levels than Ate1-containing mice (88.6 mg/dl versus 125.3 mg/dl, respectively; p<0.04), and also lower glucose levels 6 hr after administration of glucose (80.9 mg/dl versus 109.7 mg/dl, respectively; p<0.04), consistent with the (expected) higher energy expenditure of Ate1-deficient mice, and suggesting normal sensitivity of these mice to insulin (Fig. 10B). There were no other significant differences in blood composition (as well as urine composition) between Ate1-containing and Ate1-deficient mice (Tables 2 and 3).
###end p 54

Urinalysis.
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 15 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Ate1-deficient mice had a significantly lower urine pH.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 65 86 65 86 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 102 103 102 103 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 122 123 122 123 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 310 311 310 311 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 347 348 347 348 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 390 398 390 398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10E</xref>
###xml 466 467 466 467 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 498 499 498 499 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 698 706 698 706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10F</xref>
###xml 138 142 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 236 240 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 384 388 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 663 667 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To measure metabolic rate, we employed indirect calorimetry (see Materials and Methods), determining O2 consumption and CO2 production by mice under resting conditions. The metabolic rate (resting metabolic rate, RMR) of Ate1-deficient mice was indeed higher than normal: they consumed on average 46.12 ml of O2 per kg per min, versus 29.3 ml of O2 per kg per min for Ate1-containing mice (Fig. 10E). In contrast, the respiratory exchange ratio, RER (the ratio of CO2 eliminated from the lungs to O2 taken into the lungs), a parameter that depends on a preferred source of fuel (e.g., carbohydrates versus fat), was similar for Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing mice: 0.75 and 0.76, respectively (Fig. 10F).
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 144 148 144 148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Turner1">[34]</xref>
###xml 563 565 563 565 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 594 596 594 596 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 702 723 702 723 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 800 802 800 802 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 853 855 853 855 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 977 979 977 979 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 1017 1024 1017 1024 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g009">Fig. 9D</xref>
###xml 1077 1079 1077 1079 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 1161 1169 1161 1169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g009">Figs. 9C</xref>
###xml 1174 1177 1174 1177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">10D</xref>
###xml 1304 1306 1304 1306 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 4 17 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 388 392 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 537 544 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 761 765 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 884 888 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 960 964 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1011 1015 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1052 1056 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1155 1159 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1347 1351 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The S. cerevisiae N-end rule pathway regulates the import of short peptides through the conditional degradation of Cup9, the import's repressor [34]. It is likely (but remains to be verified) that the N-end rule pathway regulates the transmembrane traffic of peptides in mammals as well. To address the possibility that significantly lower weights (despite hyperphagia) of Ate1-deficient mice might stem, at least in part, from an impaired ability to import peptides and/or amino acids from their gastrointestinal (GI) tract, we labeled E. coli with a mixture of 14C-amino acids and isolated a 14C-protein fraction that was essentially free of nucleic acids, fatty acids, lipids and carbohydrates (see Materials and Methods). Ate1-deficient and Ate1-containing mice were gavaged with a bolus of this 14C-protein preparation, followed by measurements of 14C in several organs of these mice (and in their feces) as a function of time post-gavage. Ate1-deficient mice passed less 14C in feces than Ate1-containing mice (Fig. 9D). Moreover, Ate1-deficient mice accumulated more of 14C in their brains, livers, spleens, kidneys and hearts than Ate1-containing mice (Figs. 9C and 10D). Irrespective of mechanistic causes involved (they remain to be understood), higher than wild-type levels of protein-derived 14C delivered to tissues of Ate1-deficient mice indicated the absence of significant defects in their transport of peptides and/or amino acids from GI tract.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 73 83 73 83 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Figs. 6C&#8211;E</xref>
###xml 85 90 85 90 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">8A, D</xref>
###xml 95 101 95 101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">10E, F</xref>
###xml 525 533 525 533 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10G</xref>
###xml 684 692 684 692 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10G</xref>
###xml 790 794 790 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Rousseau1">[35]</xref>
###xml 1073 1084 1073 1084 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10C, G</xref>
###xml 1160 1169 1160 1169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">Fig. 7G&#8211;I</xref>
###xml 67 71 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 340 344 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 395 399 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 633 637 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 931 935 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1067 1071 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Given the metabolic and behavioral abnormalities of Ate1-deficient mice (Figs. 6C-E, 8A, D and 10E, F), we also examined them for expression of neuropeptides. As we would be interested, at present, only in strong differences, a semiquantitative RT-PCR was employed. Using total RNA from hypothalami of Ate1-deficient versus Ate1-containing mice, we found no consistent differences between these mice in regard to the levels of hypothalamic mRNAs that encoded the agouti-related protein (AgRP) and the neural peptide Y (NPY) (Fig. 10G). Strikingly, however, there was a consistent and strong decrease of expression, in Ate1-deficient mice, of mRNA encoding proopiomelanocortin (POMC) (Fig. 10G). POMC is a precursor of several neurohormones with broad systemic and brain-specific functions ([35] and refs. therein). These functions include a role in melanocyte regulation (a process that is likely to be perturbed in Ate1-deficient mice; see above) and a down-regulation of food intake (the observed deficiency in POMC is consistent with hyperphagia of Ate1-deficient mice (Fig. 10C, G)). Similarly to a connection between Ate1 and the Ucp1 uncoupling protein (Fig. 7G-I), our finding of a link between N-terminal arginylation and the expression of POMC is likely to provide an experimental route to identifying the relevant Ate1-dependent circuit.
###end p 63
###begin title 64
Discussion
###end title 64
###begin p 65
###xml 524 531 524 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g001">Fig. 1A</xref>
###xml 759 771 759 771 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s1">Introduction</xref>
A cell is alive owing to a cell-wide dynamic network of structurally or functionally interacting biopolymers. Some parts of this network can be sufficiently insulated, through their design, to be considered, in the first approximation, as distinct circuits. The N-end rule pathway is one such circuit. Its enzymes receive as their input specific degron-bearing proteins and convert them, through deamidation, arginylation, polyubiquitylation and processive degradation, into an output of proteolysis-derived short peptides (Fig. 1A). The rate and selectivity of the proteasome-mediated protein degradation by the N-end rule pathway are modulated by physiological effectors, including specific phosphokinases, short peptides, redox, heme and nitric oxide (see Introduction). Some of N-end rule substrates are produced by proteases that include MetAPs, separases, caspases and calpains. These and other nonprocessive proteases, which function as upstream components of the N-end rule pathway, have in common their ability to convert, through a cleavage, a pro-N-degron into an N-degron.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 80 87 80 87 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g001">Fig. 1A</xref>
###xml 142 146 142 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 175 179 175 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 211 215 211 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Kwon2">[10]</xref>
###xml 245 252 245 252 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s2">Results</xref>
###xml 371 375 371 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 427 438 427 438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g001">Figs. 1C, D</xref>
###xml 697 706 673 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g004">Fig. 4A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 829 836 793 800 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g004">Fig. 4B</xref>
###xml 997 1005 961 969 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10C</xref>
###xml 1054 1062 1018 1026 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g005">Figs. 5D</xref>
###xml 1067 1071 1031 1035 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">7A&#8211;E</xref>
###xml 1115 1123 1079 1087 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g010">Fig. 10E</xref>
###xml 1162 1169 1126 1133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g007">Fig. 7F</xref>
###xml 1189 1197 1153 1161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g005">Figs. 5D</xref>
###xml 1202 1204 1166 1168 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">6A</xref>
###xml 1217 1224 1181 1188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g005">Fig. 5B</xref>
###xml 1252 1262 1216 1226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Figs. 6C&#8211;E</xref>
###xml 1267 1269 1231 1233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g008">8A</xref>
###xml 1292 1301 1256 1265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g006">Fig. 6F&#8211;K</xref>
###xml 136 141 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 331 335 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 554 558 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 575 579 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 651 655 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 991 995 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1014 1018 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The present study expanded the earlier understanding of the Ate1 R-transferase (Fig. 1A) by making possible a postnatal inactivation of mouse Ate1. (Unconditional deletion of Ate1 results in embryonic lethality [10].) Described and discussed in Results is a large set of defects, some of them quite striking, in juvenile and adult mice upon the postnatal inactivation of Ate1 and the resulting loss of N-terminal arginylation (Figs. 1C, D). The initial abnormality is a rapid decrease of body weight and early death of approximately15% of Ate1-deficient mice, with surviving mice attaining, gradually, only approximately70% of the weight of wild-type mice identically treated with tamoxifen (TM) (Fig. 4A-C). Both "partial" lethality and the transiency of acute crisis, over approximately3 weeks after TM treatment (red arrow in Fig. 4B), remain to be understood in molecular terms. This crisis and subsequent failure to thrive occur despite higher than normal food intake by Ate1-deficient mice (Fig. 10C). These mice contain little or no visceral fat (Figs. 5D and 7A-E), and exhibit an increased metabolic rate (Fig. 10E), resistance to diet-induced obesity (Fig. 7F), enlarged brains (Figs. 5D and 6A), kyphosis (Fig. 5B), a striking hyperkinesia (Figs. 6C-E and 8A), and male sterility (Fig. 6F-K).
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 56 60 56 60 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Hayashi1">[25]</xref>
###xml 95 99 95 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 198 201 198 201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 194 201 194 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 202 211 202 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 250 256 250 256 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 246 256 246 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 265 268 265 268 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 261 268 261 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 286 289 286 289 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 282 289 282 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 403 410 403 410 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s2">Results</xref>
###xml 475 481 475 481 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 471 481 471 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 494 497 494 497 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 490 497 490 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 555 558 543 546 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 551 558 539 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 565 575 553 563 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g004">Fig. 4A, B</xref>
###xml 647 650 635 638 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 643 650 631 638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 815 818 803 806 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 811 818 799 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1021 1025 1009 1013 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox</sup>
###xml 1017 1025 1005 1013 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox</sup></italic>
###xml 1037 1038 1025 1026 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1033 1038 1021 1026 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 140 145 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 212 217 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 482 486 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 498 502 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 559 563 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 713 718 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 819 823 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 924 928 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Owing to current constraints of the Cre-lox technology ([25] and refs. therein), the extent of Ate1 inactivation, while nearly 100% in some mouse tissues, was variable in others. The TM-induced Ate1-/-;CaggCreER mouse strains are thus mosaics of Ate1flox/- and Ate1-/- cells, where Ate1-/- cells are a great majority in most organs, such as the brain, but even there do not reach 100% of all cells (see Results). The initial weight loss upon the TM-induced conversion of Ate1flox/- mice to Ate1-/- mice was accompanied by death of approximately15% of Ate1-/- mice (Fig. 4A, B). Such a "partially" lethal phenotype suggests that an adult-onset Ate1-/- genotype in all cells (as distinguished from most cells) of a mouse might be incompatible with viability, similarly to the embryonic lethality of unconditional Ate1-/- mice. Thus, paradoxically, the discovery, in the present study, of specific Ate1-linked defects in adult mice might have been made possible by incomplete penetrance of the Cre-induced conversion of Ate1flox to the Ate1- allele.
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 274 286 274 286 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s1">Introduction</xref>
###xml 351 354 351 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Varshavsky2">[2]</xref>
###xml 542 546 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The set of definitively identified mammalian N-end rule substrates that involve N-terminal arginylation consists, at present, of fewer than 10 proteins. They subserve different functions, from chromosome segregation to control of apoptosis and regulation of G proteins (see Introduction). This set is the tip of the iceberg, as several considerations [2], in addition to our findings above, strongly suggest a larger number of physiological Ate1 substrates. Given this complexity, the specific and often striking phenotypes of Ate1-deficient mice that were discovered in the present work will be of major assistance in deciphering the underlying Ate1 circuits.
###end p 68
###begin title 69
Methods
###end title 69
###begin title 70
Animal Care and Treatments
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 335 339 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 536 540 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 625 631 <span type="species:ncbi:4182">sesame</span>
###xml 691 695 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 797 801 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
All animal care and procedures in the present study were conducted according to the relevant NIH guidelines, and were approved (Protocol #1328) by the Institutional Animal Care and Use Committee, the Office of Laboratory Animal Research (OLAR) at the California Institute of Technology, where the entire present study was carried out. Mice were housed at approximately22degreesC, at a pathogen-free (barrier) facility, using a 12 hr light/12 hr dark cycle, with Laboratory Rodent Diet 5001 (PMI International, Richmond, IN) ad libitum. Mice aged between 3 and 8 weeks were treated with tamoxifen (TM) (Sigma) (2 mg in 0.2 ml sesame oil) by daily intraperitoneal (IP) injections over 5 days. Mice were weighed weekly, starting 3 days before the first TM treatment. For a high-fat diet (HFD) study, mice were fed ad libitum a diet containing 35.5% fat (BioServe, Frenchtown, NJ), and were weighed weekly.
###end p 71
###begin title 72

###xml 829 832 745 748 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">iii</bold>

###xml 1058 1061 950 953 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PGK</sub>
###xml 1058 1061 950 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>PGK</sub></italic>
###xml 1071 1075 963 967 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Joyner1">[36]</xref>
###xml 1078 1079 970 971 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</bold>
###xml 1118 1122 998 1002 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 1186 1188 1066 1068 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">vi</bold>
###xml 1274 1277 1154 1157 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PGK</sub>
###xml 1274 1277 1154 1157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>PGK</sub></italic>
###xml 1736 1740 1613 1617 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Nagy1">[37]</xref>
###xml 2119 2123 1979 1983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 2132 2143 1992 2003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Figs. 2C, D</xref>
###xml 2269 2275 2129 2135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Fig. 2</xref>
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 1529 1535 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 1787 1792 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Mouse genomic DNA encoding Ate1 was isolated from a BAC library [10]. Two pBluescript-based plasmids were used to construct the targeting vector. In one insert, a approximately12 kb HindIII fragment contained Ate1 exons 1a, 1b, 2, and 3 as well as approximately1.9 kb of DNA 3' of exon 3 (ending just before exon 4). In the other insert, a approximately2.9 kb fragment contained Ate1 exons 4 and 5. The entire approximately12 kb HindIII fragment and a part of the approximately2.9 kb fragment were modified as described below and assembled into a final approximately22.5 kb targeting vector consisting of the following parts (Fig. 2C): (i) pBR322 backbone (New England Biolabs, Ipswich, MA); (ii) a approximately6.3 kb "long arm" of Ate1 homology containing the Ate1 exon 1a, the bidirectional PAte1 promoter [14], and exon 1b; (iii) A single loxP site approximately300 bp upstream of Ate1 exon 2; (iv) a approximately2 kb fragment that contains, 50 bp downstream of Ate1 exon 4, a "floxed" Hph (hygromycin) antibiotic-resistance marker, expressed from the PPGK promoter [36]; (v) a approximately1.2 kb "short arm" of Ate1 homology that spans most of the intron between exons 4 and 5; (vi) a gene encoding HSV-TK (herpes simplex virus thymidine kinase), expressed from the PPGK promoter. The targeting vector was linearized with BamHI and electroporated into CJ7 embryonic stem (ES) cells (a gift from Dr. Thomas Gridley, formerly of Jackson Laboratories, Bar Harbor, ME). ES cells were grown in DMEM supplemented with 15% fetal bovine serum (FBS), 0.1 mM non-essential amino acids, 0.1 mM beta-mercaptoethanol, 2 mM glutamine, 100 U/ml penicillin, 0.1 mg/ml streptomycin, 1 mM pyruvate, and 1,000 U/ml leukemia inhibitory factor (LIF) [37], using a feeder layer of hygromycin-resistant mouse primary fibroblasts that had been treated with 10 microg/ml mitomycin C for 3 hr at 37degreesC. Selection with hygromycin (at 0.2 mg/ml) and 1-(2'-deoxy, 2'-fluoro-beta-D-arabinofuranosyl)-5-iodouracil (FIAU; at 0.4 microM) was started 24 hr after electroporation. Correctly targeted ES cell clones that contained "tri-loxed" Ate1 allele (Figs. 2C, D) were identified using Southern hybridization and PCR. Southern DNA probes and positions of primers for PCR are indicated in Fig. 2.
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 371 375 371 375 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Joyner1">[36]</xref>
###xml 377 381 377 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Nair1">[38]</xref>
###xml 461 465 461 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 540 543 540 543 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PGK</sub>
###xml 540 543 540 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>PGK</sub></italic>
###xml 544 547 544 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hph</italic>
###xml 558 565 558 565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Fig. 2D</xref>
###xml 607 611 607 611 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 728 732 728 732 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Leneuve1">[39]</xref>
###xml 734 738 734 738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Lakso1">[40]</xref>
###xml 740 744 740 744 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Holzenberger1">[41]</xref>
###xml 777 781 777 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">loxP</italic>
###xml 810 814 810 814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 949 953 949 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">loxP</italic>
###xml 1023 1032 1023 1032 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Fig. 2A&#8211;F</xref>
###xml 1106 1110 1106 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">loxP</italic>
###xml 1118 1125 1118 1125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Fig. 2E</xref>
###xml 1253 1256 1253 1256 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PGK</sub>
###xml 1253 1256 1253 1256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>PGK</sub></italic>
###xml 1257 1260 1257 1260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hph</italic>
###xml 1294 1300 1294 1300 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox/+</sup>
###xml 1290 1300 1290 1300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 420 425 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 648 652 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1048 1053 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1148 1152 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1185 1189 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Two correctly targeted, independently produced ES cell lines that had apparently normal karyotypes were injected into 3.5-days-postcoitum C57BL/6J blastocysts and implanted into pseudopregnant females. The resulting male chimeric offspring were mated with C57BL/6J females. In some of the progeny, "floxed" ES cells became a part of germ line. Standard mating techniques [36], [38] were then used to produce, initially, mouse strains that contained a "tri-lox" Ate1 configuration, in that they also contained the floxed positive-selection PPGK-hph cassette (Fig. 2D). This DNA segment was removed by mating Ate1-tri-lox heterozygotes with EIIa-Cre mice that expressed Cre recombinase only in early, pre-implantation blastocysts [39], [40], [41]. Owing to the presence of three loxP sites at the initial floxed Ate1 locus, F1 progeny from this cross were mosaic, i.e., their tissues, including germ line, contained varying configurations of retained loxP sites, depending on specific patterns of Cre-mediated recombination (Fig. 2A-F). To isolate a mouse strain with the desired configuration of (retained) loxP sites (Fig. 2E), the above F1 mosaic mice were mated to wild-type C57BL/6 mice. This produced, among other progeny, a strain that lacked the PPGK-Hph cassette and had the desired Ate1flox/+ genotype, in the (mixed) C75BL/6J-129SvEv background.
###end p 74

###xml 1284 1291 1284 1291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
