###xml 1407 1414 1407 1414 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Fig. 2E</xref>
###xml 1444 1448 1444 1448 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox</sup>
###xml 1440 1448 1440 1448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox</sup></italic>
###xml 1515 1522 1515 1522 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Fig. 2F</xref>
###xml 1537 1538 1537 1538 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1533 1538 1533 1538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 116 120 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 156 160 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 330 334 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 552 557 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 725 733 <span type="species:ncbi:10678">phage P1</span>
###xml 774 779 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 995 999 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1021 1025 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1049 1053 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1122 1126 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1164 1168 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1190 1194 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1221 1225 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1274 1278 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1302 1306 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Through the use of appropriate mating pairs, with genotyping of resulting progeny, we produced Ate1flox/-;CaggCreER mice as well as Ate1flox/flox;CaggCreER mice (Fig. 2). The former strain harbored one unconditionally null Ate1- allele (derived, through matings, from the previously constructed unconditional heterozygous Ate1+/- mice [10]) and one "floxed", conditionally active Ate1flox allele that could be made null in the presence of active Cre recombinase. In the latter strain (Ate1flox/flox;CaggCreER), both copies of Ate1 were Ate1flox. These mouse strains also contained the CaggCreER gene, expressed from the ubiquitously active chimeric Cagg promoter (Fig. 2E) [25]. CaggCreER encoded CreER, a fusion between the phage P1 Cre recombinase and a derivative of the mouse estrogen receptor ligand binding domain. CreER was functionally inactive (sequestered in the cytosol) but could be activated by intraperitoneal (IP) injection of tamoxifen (TM) [25]. To produce Ate1flox/-;CaggCreER mice, we mated Ate1flox/+ mice with Ate1+/-;CaggCreER mice (the latter were generated by mating Ate1+/- with Ate1+/+;CaggCreER mice). To produce Ate1flox/flox;CaggCreER mice, we mated Ate1flox/+ mice with Ate1flox/+;CaggCreER mice (the latter were generated by mating Ate1flox/+ mice with Ate1+/+;CaggCreER mice). In the notations here and elsewhere in the paper, "flox-on" indicates a configuration depicted in Fig. 2E (the functionally active Ate1flox allele), whereas "flox-off" indicates a configuration depicted in Fig. 2F (the null Ate1- allele).
###end p 75
###begin title 76
Southern Hybridization and PCR
###end title 76
###begin p 77
###xml 415 417 409 411 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 418 421 412 415 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0.1</sub>
###xml 900 902 888 890 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 903 906 891 894 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0.1</sub>
###xml 501 506 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Total genomic DNA was isolated from ES cells by washing them twice with phosphate-buffered saline PBS, followed by an overnight incubation at 50degreesC in 10 mM EDTA, 10 mM NaCl, 0.5% Sarcosyl,10 mM Tris-HCl (pH 7.5) containing Proteinase K at 0.2 mg/ml. Thereafter an equal volume of 75 mM NaCl in 100% ethanol was added. Precipitated genomic DNA was then gently washed twice with 70% ethanol and resuspended in T10E0.1 buffer (10 mM Tris (pH 8.0), 0.1 mM EDTA). Total genomic DNA was isolated from mouse tails or other tissues by overnight incubation at 55degreesC, with constant rotation, in 5 mM EDTA, 0.2 M NaCl, 0.3% SDS, 0.1 M Tris (pH 8.5) containing Proteinase K at 0.4 mg/ml. Thereafter an equal volume of isopropanol was added, and the mixture was gently inverted several times. Genomic DNA was then precipitated, and washed twice, with 70% ethanol, followed by a gentle resuspension in T10E0.1 buffer.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 50 54 50 54 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Ausubel1">[42]</xref>
###xml 63 65 63 65 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 165 172 165 172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 276 283 276 283 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 405 411 405 411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007757-g002">Fig. 2</xref>
###xml 443 445 443 445 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 75 80 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Southern hybridization was performed as described [42], with a 32P-labeled mouse DNA probes that was produced by PCR using the following primers: CB108F and CB107R (Table 2) to amplify a 219 bp genomic fragment containing Ate1 exon 5 (probe D, external probe); CB23 and CB24 (Table 4) to amplify a 929 bp genomic fragment that was a part of the long arm of the targeting vector (Probe A, internal probe) (Fig. 2). DNA probes were labeled with 32P-labeled using the Rediprime-II Random Prime Labeling System (Amersham Biosciences, Piscataway, NJ) according to the manufacturer's protocol. Hybridization with Probe A was carried out overnight at 57degreesC in ExpressHyb solution (Clontech). The membrane was then washed once for 10 min at room temperature (RT) in 2xSSC/0.1% SDS, once for 30 min at 55degreesC in 2xSSC/0.1% SDS, once for 30 minutes at 58degreesC in 0.5xSSC/0.1% SDS, and once for 30 minutes at 65degreesC in 0.1xSSC/0.1% SDS, followed by autoradiography. (1xSSC is 0.15 M NaCl, 15 mM Na-citrate, pH 7.4.) Hybridization with Probe D was carried out overnight at 55degreesC in ExpressHyb solution (Clontech). The membrane was then washed once for 10 min at RT in 2xSSC/0.1% SDS, once for 30 min at 55degreesC in 2xSSC/0.1% SDS, and once for 30 min at 58degreesC in 1xSSC/0.1% SDS, followed by autoradiography.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
PCR primers used in the present study.
###end title 79
###begin title 80
###xml 14 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Genotyping of Mouse Strains
###end title 80
###begin p 81
###xml 167 171 167 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1</italic>
###xml 314 321 314 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 387 391 387 391 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox</sup>
###xml 383 391 383 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox</sup></italic>
###xml 468 469 468 469 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 464 469 464 469 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 555 562 555 562 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 628 632 628 632 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flox</sup>
###xml 624 632 624 632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>flox</sup></italic>
###xml 645 646 645 646 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 641 646 641 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 712 716 712 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Il-2</italic>
###xml 781 788 781 788 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 861 862 861 862 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 857 862 857 862 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 870 874 870 874 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Kwon2">[10]</xref>
###xml 918 919 918 919 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 914 919 914 919 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 998 1005 998 1005 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 1060 1069 1060 1069 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1132 1133 1132 1133 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1128 1133 1128 1133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ate1<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1191 1200 1191 1200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 1513 1522 1495 1504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CaggCreER</italic>
###xml 82 87 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 145 150 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
PCR-based genotyping was carried out with total genomic DNA isolated from various mouse tissues. Routine genotyping was performed using DNA from mouse tails. Specific Ate1 alleles and transgenes encoding specific derivatives of Cre were identified as follows. A two-primer PCR using the CB156F and CB157R primers (Table 4) was employed to produce and detect a 512 bp fragment of the Ate1flox ("floxON", active) allele as well as a 472 bp fragment of the wild-type Ate1+ allele. A four-primer PCR using the CB110F, CB157R, OIMR0042, and OIM0043 primers Z (Table 4) was employed to produce and detect a 470 bp fragment of the Ate1flox-derived Ate1- allele ("floxOFF") as well as a (control) 324 bp fragment of the Il-2 gene. A three-primer PCR using the AK49, YT641, and AK83-CBfix (Table 4) was employed to detect both a 300 bp fragment of the unconditional Ate1- allele [10] and a 560-bp fragment of the wild-type Ate1+ allele. A four-primer PCR using the Cre-1, Cre-2, CB159R, and CB160F primers (Table 4) was employed to detect both a 320 bp fragment of the CaggCreER transgene as well as a 1,060 bp fragment of the wild-type Ate1+ allele. All PCR reactions except for those to detect the CaggCreER transgene were carried out using HotStar Taq DNA polymerase, standard buffer conditions (Qiagen, Valencia, CA), 35 cycles of template denaturation for 30 seconds at 95degreesC, followed by primer annealing for 30 seconds at 60degreesC and primer extension for 1 minute at 72degreesC. PCR reactions for detecting CaggCreER were carried out using 30 cycles of template denaturation for 30 seconds at 95degreesC, followed by primer annealing for 30 seconds at 58degreesC and primer extension for 45 seconds at 72degreesC.
###end p 81
###begin title 82
Northern and RT-PCR Analyses of RNA
###end title 82
###begin p 83
###xml 478 485 478 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007757-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 36 41 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Total RNA was isolated from various mouse tissues using the RNeasy Protect Mini Kit (Qiagen). Tissue disruption and homogenization were done in Buffer RLT and the MP FastPrep-24 instrument with Lysing Matrix D (MP Biomedicals, Solon, OH) for 2 runs at 6.5 m/s. First-strand cDNA was primed with oligo-dT using the SuperScript III First-Strand Synthesis System (Invitrogen, Carlsbad, CA) and PCR was carried out using primers cited in legends to the corresponding figures and in Table 4.
###end p 83
###begin title 84
Tissue Extracts and Immunoblotting
###end title 84
###begin p 85
###xml 491 492 491 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 8 13 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Various mouse tissues were harvested and lysed in "Tissue Lysis Buffer" (10% glycerol, 0.05% NP40, 0.15 M NaCl, 2 mM EDTA, 1 mM dithiothreitol (DTT) 1 mM phenylmethylsulfonyl fluoride PMSF 50 mM HEPES, pH 7.5) plus freshly dissolved "Complete EDTA-Free Protease Inhibitors" (Roche), using the MP FastPrep-24 instrument and Lysing Matrix D (MP Biomedicals, with 2 or 3 runs at 6.5 m/s for 25 sec each, and with 5-min incubations on ice between the runs. The lysates were centrifuged at 10,000g for 20 min at 4degreesC. The supernatants were fractionated by SDS-12.5% PAGE, transferred to Immobilon-P PVDF membranes (Millipore, Billerica, MA), and analyzed by immunoblotting (IB) with antibodies indicated in specific figures. Immunoblots were visualized using SuperSignal West Pico or SuperSignal West Dura reagents (Thermo Scientific, Rockford, IL) according to the manufacturer's instructions.
###end p 85
###begin title 86
###xml 18 23 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Other Analyses of Mouse Tissues
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 72 73 72 73 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 9 14 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 188 193 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Specific mouse tissues were dissected immediately after euthanasia by CO2 inhalation. The tissues washed with PBS, blotted dry on Kimwipes, and weighed (wet). For dry-weight measurements, mouse brains were dissected intact, washed in PBS, blotted dry on Kimwipes, weighed wet, then incubated overnight in acetone. After acetone incubation, individual brains were lyophilized until their (dry) weight no longer decreased.
###end p 87
###begin p 88
###xml 137 141 137 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Nagy1">[37]</xref>
###xml 361 362 358 359 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 472 473 463 464 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 787 788 778 779 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 891 892 876 877 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 898 899 883 884 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 910 911 895 896 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 917 918 902 903 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
For routine histological examinations, tissues or organs were fixed in Bouin's solution or in 4% formaldehyde, using standard procedures [37]. Fixed samples were embedded in paraffin, sectioned, and stained with hematoxylin and eosin. To stain for LacZ (NLS-betagal), dissected tissues or organs were fixed in LacZfix (0.2% glutaraldehyde, 5 mM EGTA, 0.1 M MgCl2 in PBS (pH 7.3)) for 4 hr, rinsed twice with PBS, dehydrated overnight at 4degreesC in 30% sucrose, 2 mM MgCl2 in PBS, and embedded and frozen in Tissue-Tek O.C.T. Compound (Sakura Finetek USA, Inc. Torrance, CA). Cryosections (prepared using a Tissue Tek Microtome/Cryostat model 4553) were mounted onto glass slides, fixed in LacZfix for 10 min at RT, washed 3 times in LacZWash (0.02% NP40, 01% Na-deoxycholate, 2 mM MgCl2 in PBS), and stained overnight at 37degreesC with LacZ stain (LacZWash containing 1 mg/ml XGal, 5 mM K4Fe(CN)6 and 5 mM K3Fe(CN)6). Stained sections were washed with PBS and mounted with Permount for light microscopy. Apoptosis was assessed by TUNEL, a nuclear DNA fragmentation assay, using a TUNEL kit (Roche, Indianapolis, IN), fluorescein-dUTP, and manufacturer's instructions. Cell proliferation was assayed using the Click-It Edu Cell Proliferation kit (Invitrogen).
###end p 88
###begin title 89
In Vitro Arginylation Assay
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 183 187 175 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Hu3">[14]</xref>
###xml 376 377 368 369 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 441 442 430 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sup>
###xml 694 695 677 678 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 729 730 712 713 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 788 789 765 766 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 894 895 871 872 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sup>
###xml 95 100 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 208 215 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 248 255 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The arginyl-transferase (R-transferase) reaction (50 microl) contained extracts for a specific mouse tissue (2.5 mg of total protein per ml), alpha-lactalbumin (arginylation reporter [14]) (0.5 mg/ml), total E. coli tRNA (0.6 mg/ml) (Sigma), total E. coli aminoacyl-tRNA synthetases (800 U/ml) (Sigma), 5 mM MG132 (proteasome inhibitor) (Sigma), 1 mM ATP, 30 mM KCl, 2 mM MgCl2, 2 mM beta-mercaptoethanol, 10 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0) and 0.3 mM 3H-arginine (PerkinElmer, NEN Radiochemicals, Waltham, MA). The reaction mixture was incubated for 30 min at 37degreesC and deposited onto GF/C filter disks (GE-Healthcare, Pittsburg, PA). The filters were thereafter incubated for 10 min in 10% cold CCl3COOH, followed by 10 min in 5% CCl3COOH at 95degreesC. The filters were then washed in 5% CCl3COOH 3 times at RT, followed by a single ether:ethanol (1:1) wash, two ether washes, and measurements of 3H retained on a filter using a scintillation spectrometer.
###end p 90
###begin title 91
Blood and Urine Analyses
###end title 91
###begin p 92
###xml 270 271 258 259 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 31 36 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Blood (approximately0.6 ml per mouse) was withdrawn by cardiac puncture and transferred into BD Microtainer SST tubes (BD, Franklin Lakes, NJ). The serum fraction was prepared by centrifugation in a microcentrifuge after clotting occurred, immediately frozen in liquid N2 and stored at -80degreesC. The levels of glucose, cholesterol, sodium, potassium, chloride, calcium, phosphorus, blood urea nitrogen, creatine, total protein, albumin, total bilirubin, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), alkaline phosphatase, gamma-glutamyltransferase (gamma gt), as well as the T3 and T4 hormones were determined by Phoenix Central Laboratories (Everett, WA).
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 113 117 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 182 186 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Urine was obtained by placing the external urethra over a test tube. Urine samples collected from Ate1-deficient mice were pooled and compared with pooled urine from Ate1-containing mice. The levels of glucose, bilirubin, ketones, blood, protein, urobilinogen, nitrite, leukocytes, as well as the pH and specific gravity were determined using the Multistix 10 SG Reagent Strips (Bayer, Tarry Town, NY).
###end p 93
###begin title 94
Measurements of Body Temperature and Cold Sensitivity
###end title 94
###begin p 95
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 20 25 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Mice (housed at one mouse per cage, without bedding but with food and water) were exposed to a 4degreesC environment for up to 6 hr Their core body temperature was monitored every 30 min via a rectal probe digital thermometer (Thermalert TH-8; Physitemp Instruments., Clifton, NJ).
###end p 95
###begin title 96
###xml 16 18 16 18 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
Measurements of 14C-Protein Uptake from Gastrointestinal Tract
###end title 96
###begin p 97
###xml 103 105 95 97 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 133 135 125 127 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 226 228 206 208 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 462 463 436 437 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 666 668 640 642 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 796 798 770 772 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">14</sup>
###xml 0 7 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 678 685 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 708 713 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 887 892 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
E. coli DH5alpha cells were grown in minimal M9 media supplemented with 0.5% glucose and 50 microCi of 14C-amino acids (derived from 14C-protein hydrolysate (Amersham)) until the incorporation of approximately70% of the added 14C amino acids. Cells were lysed by one freeze/thaw cycle in PBS containing 1 mg/ml lysozyme and incubated with RNase H and DNase I for 45 min at 37degreesC. A crude protein fraction was isolated by precipitation with cold 10% TCA (CCl3COOH), and the pellet was washed with ice-cold acetone. The pellet was redissolved in PBS, with a brief sonication to facilitate solubilization. 0.2 ml of the resulting sample, containing 260,000 cpm of 14C-labeled E. coli proteins was fed to a mouse by oral gavage. Urine and feces was collected at various times post-gavage. Total 14C was measured, using a scintillation spectrometer, in feces, urine, and (eventually) in mouse tissue samples that were collected either 48 hr or 15 days post-gavage.
###end p 97
###begin title 98
Measurements of Glucose Uptake
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 22 26 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
For glucose analyses, mice were fasted for 24 hr, then gavaged with 50 mg glucose in 0.2 ml of water. Blood was collected through the lateral tail vein at 15, 30, 60, 90, 120, and 360 min post-gavage. Blood glucose levels were determined using the OneTouch UltraMini Blood Glucose Monitoring System (LifeScan, Johnson and Johnson, Milpitas, CA).
###end p 99
###begin title 100
Metabolic Analyses
###end title 100
###begin p 101
###xml 199 203 199 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Wasserman1">[43]</xref>
###xml 205 209 205 209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Dauger1">[44]</xref>
###xml 49 54 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 218 222 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The resting metabolic rate was determined at the Mouse Physiology Laboratory in the Department of Physiology at the Geffen School of Medicine, UCLA using indirect calorimetry as previously described [43], [44]. Single mice were placed into a custom-made enclosed plexiglas chamber (25 cmx12 cmx7.5 cm, with 4 room air intake vents and one outflow port) and allowed to come to rest over a period of 30 min to 2 hr. Outflow of expired gases was sampled by the gas analyzer and recorded using a computerized acquisition system during a 30-min resting interval.
###end p 101
###begin title 102
###xml 16 21 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
MRI Analyses of Mouse Brains
###end title 102
###begin p 103
###xml 70 74 70 74 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Redwine1">[45]</xref>
###xml 962 966 946 950 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Shattuck1">[46]</xref>
###xml 76 80 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 209 213 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 345 350 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 780 784 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The procedures used were essentially the same as previously described [45]. Mice were given an IP injection of 40 mg/kg of Na-pentobarbital (Nembutal, Hospira, Inc., Lake Forest, IL). Once fully anesthetized, mice were transcardially perfused with 4% formaldehyde in PBS. MRI analysis was performed by the Caltech Brain Imaging Center. Briefly, mouse heads were excised and postfixed in 4% formaldehyde/PBS overnight. Hair and skin were removed from fixed heads, which were then soaked in 5 mM Gadolinium-based MR contrast agent (Prohance Bracco Diagnostics, Durham, NC) for 10 days, to decrease the intrinsic tissue relaxation rates and improve the MR acquisition efficiency. A gradient echo sequence (TE/TR = 8 msec/50 msec, 16 averages) was used to acquire 3D data sets of the mice heads, using a Bruker 7T Biospec animal magnet system. Images were reconstructed with an isotropic resolution of approximately90 microm and analyzed using Brainsuite 2 software [46].
###end p 103
###begin title 104
Open-Field and Startle Response Tests
###end title 104
###begin p 105
###xml 127 128 127 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x</italic>
###xml 133 134 133 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">y</italic>
###xml 314 318 314 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007757-Geyer1">[47]</xref>
###xml 53 57 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
For the open-field activity measurements, individual mice were placed into a square chamber (50 by 50 cm). Movements along the x and y axes were tracked and analyzed using Ethovision software (Noldus, Leesburg, VA) over 15-min intervals. Startle response tests were carried out essentially as described previously [47].
###end p 105
###begin p 106
###xml 436 441 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
